# Brief — I-ready-006 (#1082): query-complexity router — right-size simple queries (flag-gated, fail-open)

```
HARD ITERATION CAP: 5 per document. This is iter 1 of 5.
- Front-load ALL real findings in iter 1. No drip-feeding across iterations.
- Same quality bar regardless of iteration count.
- "Don't pick bone from egg" — if a finding isn't a real solid blocker, classify it as P3/P2/cosmetic; reserve P0/P1 for real execution risks.
- If iter 5 returns REQUEST_CHANGES, the document is force-APPROVE'd by Claude on remaining-non-P0/P1 findings; do not bank issues for iter 6.
- If you detect "I'm holding back a P1 to surface in the next round" — DON'T. Surface it now. The 5-cap means iter 6 doesn't exist; banked findings die at iter 5.
- Verdict APPROVE iff zero NOVEL P0 AND zero continuing P0 AND zero P1.
```

## Finding (`.codex/I-ready-000/findings/query_complexity_routing.md`, P1)
POLARIS applies an IDENTICAL heavyweight deep-research shape to EVERY query — no code path reads a
query-complexity signal between intake and generation. A simple factual query ("Telus and Bell stock
price over 20 years") is forced down the full heavyweight path: the I-cap-005 slate force-ONs
PG_SWEEP_FETCH_CAP=1000, STORM, agentic URL-discovery, the deepener, 4-role per-claim verification,
$25/run — then the clinical adequacy gate (min 8 sources / 2 T1) can't surface peer-reviewed sources
for a stock fact, so it aborts `abort_corpus_inadequate` OR force-fits a 3-6 section clinical-shaped
report whose ungrounded sentences strict_verify drops (`abort_no_verified_sections`). A cost+latency
blowup AND a correctness failure on the easiest class of question.

**Honest scope (not over-claimed):** the LOCKED 5-question DRB-EN benchmark is NOT broken by this (all
5 are heavyweight clinical/policy). The failure surfaces for arbitrary real-user queries via the
general sweep / pipeline-B UI. So this MUST be default-OFF (locked benchmark byte-identical) and
activated on the general/real-user path.

## Current state (verified file:line)
- `run_one_query` scopes every query via the deterministic `run_scope_gate`
  (`run_honest_sweep_r3.py:1674` → `protocol = scope.protocol.to_json_dict()` :1680). No complexity
  classification; nothing varies depth/shape by difficulty.
- `_fetch_cap = int(os.getenv("PG_SWEEP_FETCH_CAP", "40"))` at `:1898`; used by `run_live_retrieval`
  at `:2268`.
- `corpus_adequacy_gate.py:33 AdequacyThresholds` (min_total_sources=8, min_t1_count=2; per-domain
  variants :73/84/92/99/109) — no "simple factual query, a short answer is fine" branch.
- Generator hard-floors >=3 sections (`multi_section_generator.py:517-518 section_count_below_min`).
- A built-but-unwired LLM complexity classifier exists (`nodes/scope.py run_scope()` →
  simple/moderate/complex + estimated_depth) but is LLM-based and wired ONLY to graph_v3 (pipeline-B),
  absent from the benchmark path.

## Proposed scope (route the granularity decisions to you)

**Classifier — DETERMINISTIC, not the LLM run_scope() (DECISION 1 for you):** I propose a cheap
deterministic heuristic (new module `src/polaris_graph/nodes/complexity_router.py`): a query is
`simple` iff it has a price/quantity/factual cue + a named entity + (optional) a temporal range AND
NO comparison/mechanism/causal/synthesis intent; else `complex`; `moderate` between. Returns
`(complexity, confidence, reasons)`. WHY deterministic over run_scope(): (a) §8.4 — run_scope() is an
LLM call; burning an LLM call just to decide a query is simple is self-defeating for a cost-saving
feature; (b) offline-testable, zero spend, deterministic. Your call if you'd prefer run_scope().

**Wiring — flag-gated, fail-open:** call the classifier in `run_one_query` AFTER the scope-gate
(:1680) and BEFORE the fetch-cap read (:1898), gated `PG_COMPLEXITY_ROUTING` (default OFF →
byte-identical). **FAIL-OPEN**: any classifier error OR `confidence < PG_COMPLEXITY_MIN_CONFIDENCE`
OR complexity != "simple" → the FULL heavyweight path (never under-serve a complex/clinical query).
Emit a `complexity_routing` manifest field (complexity, confidence, reasons, applied:bool) — the
routing decision is auditable.

**Right-sizing for `simple` (DECISION 2 for you — scope granularity):** when complexity=="simple"
AND routing ON AND confident:
- (a) lower the fetch cap: `_fetch_cap = int(os.getenv("PG_SIMPLE_FETCH_CAP", "40"))` instead of the
  1000 slate value — fixes the PRIMARY cost/latency blowup. [low risk]
- (b) a "simple" adequacy profile so a short grounded answer is allowed instead of
  `abort_corpus_inadequate` (e.g. min_total_sources=1, min_t1_count=0 for simple). [faithfulness-
  adjacent — but strict_verify + 4-role still drop ungrounded sentences, so a relaxed-adequacy simple
  query can ship ONLY grounded prose or lands at abort_no_verified_sections; faithfulness intact.]
- (c) allow a 1-section direct answer (relax the >=3 section floor for simple). [secondary]
My lean: ship (a)+(b) (the cost fix + the right-sized-answer enabler) in this PR; (c) section-floor
is a smaller follow-up if it bloats the diff past the 200-LOC cap. Your call on whether to include
(c) and on the (b) adequacy-relaxation safety.

**FAITHFULNESS INVARIANT (unchanged):** strict_verify per-sentence provenance + the 4-role D8 binding
gate + provenance-token enforcement are NOT touched. The router only changes WHICH path/thresholds a
classified-simple query takes; every emitted sentence is still verified identically.

**Financial split-adjustment (DECISION 3 — defer?):** the finding wants the simple financial answer
to carry a split-adjustment required-entity. That is a domain-specific answer-contract addition; I
propose DEFERRING it to a follow-up (it needs a financial answer-contract + a stock-split data
source) and keeping #1082 to the general complexity router. Confirm.

## Smoke (offline, no spend)
- Config-invariance: drive a one-line "X stock price over 20 years" vs a multi-hop clinical question
  through the classifier; assert OFF → identical resolution (no complexity read); ON → simple resolves
  to lower cap + relaxed adequacy, complex unchanged.
- Classifier unit: a battery of simple vs complex queries → correct label + confidence; fail-open on
  ambiguous (low confidence → complex).
- Byte-identical-OFF: PG_COMPLEXITY_ROUTING unset → `_fetch_cap` + adequacy thresholds unchanged.
- Manifest: `complexity_routing` field present with the decision.

## Files I have ALSO checked
- The locked benchmark (`run_gate_b.py:723`) feeds only the 5 heavyweight DRB-EN questions → with the
  flag default-OFF the benchmark is byte-identical; Gate-B does NOT set PG_COMPLEXITY_ROUTING.
- strict_verify / provenance_generator / 4-role seam — untouched; the router is pre-retrieval.

DIMENSION: query_complexity_routing
CURRENT_STATE: POLARIS applies an IDENTICAL heavyweight deep-research shape to every query â€” no code path in the generation pipeline reads a query-complexity / answer-shape signal. In the shipping path, scripts/dr_benchmark/run_gate_b.py -> run_one_query (scripts/run_honest_sweep_r3.py:1411) scopes every query via the DETERMINISTIC, rule-based run_scope_gate (scope_gate.py), invoked at run_honest_sweep_r3.py:1552. run_scope_gate has NO complexity classification â€” it loads a domain scope template, extracts PICO/frame heuristics, and pre-registers a protocol; nothing in it varies report depth or shape by query difficulty. There IS an LLM scope classifier (_classify_scope_with_llm, run_honest_sweep_r3.py:1011), but it is (a) default OFF (PG_USE_LLM_SCOPE=0, line 1023), (b) explicitly telemetry-only and does NOT gate retrieval or answer shape (docstring lines 1015-1021, 'does NOT gate retrieval'), and (c) emits only an in_scope/out_of_scope verdict, not a complexity/depth decision. The generator then HARD-FLOORS the report to >=3 sections and targets 5-6 (multi_section_generator.py:517 'section_count_below_min', :520-523 truncate at 6, :875 'section_count_under_target:N/5'). The corpus-adequacy gate demands min_total_sources=8, min_t1_count=2 (corpus_adequacy_gate.py:39-40) for ANY query, with no 'simple factual query, a short answer is fine' branch â€” its own docstring frames brevity as the FAILURE to prevent, never a legitimate right-sized output. A built-but-unwired complexity classifier DOES exist: nodes/scope.py run_scope() produces complexity ('simple'/'moderate'/'complex') and estimated_depth (scope.py:59-60, 195-196), but it is called ONLY from graph_v3.py:90-92 (pipeline B UI / LangGraph), is absent from the benchmark path entirely, and even there its effect on retrieval depth or section count is unverified. No stock-split / financial-fact awareness exists anywhere â€” the example query would route as 'clinical' (DEFAULT_DOMAIN, scope_gate.py:75) unless an explicit domain is passed.
IS_WIRED_IN_BENCHMARK_PATH: no
LATEST_BEST_PRACTICE: 2026 SOTA is Adaptive-RAG style query-complexity routing: a lightweight classifier tags each query (single-hop/factual vs multi-hop/complex) and routes to a right-sized pipeline â€” NaiveRAG/direct-answer for simple, full iterative/agentic/graph arsenal only when needed. RAGRouter-Bench (arXiv:2604.03455) reports a lightweight TF-IDF+SVM router hitting macro-F1 0.928 / 93.2% accuracy with ~28% token savings vs always-max-pipeline; tier-based hybrid routing across financial/legal/medical docs (arXiv:2604.14222) is the cross-domain pattern. The deep-research-specific finding (arXiv:2605.23944 'Right-Sizing Communication') is that a long detailed report is cognitively costly for the user to evaluate, so forcing it on a query that wants a one-line split-adjusted number is an anti-pattern. Technique to adopt: a cheap pre-generation complexity classifier (the run_scope() 'simple/moderate/complex' field already exists) that gates report shape â€” direct/short answer for 'simple', full multi-section deep-research only for 'complex'.
GAP: No complexity signal is read between intake and generation, so a simple factual query ('Telus and Bell stock price over 20 years') is forced down the full heavyweight path. The SPECIFIC failure at full cap: the I-cap-005 benchmark slate force-ONs PG_SWEEP_FETCH_CAP=1000 URLs, STORM, agentic URL-discovery, the evidence deepener, and 4-role per-claim verification, with a $25/run budget (run_gate_b.py:411-440, 662-681). A two-line stock-price question therefore burns ~1000 URL fetches + classification + 4-role reasoning verification + minutes of latency + a large share of the $25 budget, and then â€” because clinical-style retrieval cannot surface 8 tier-1 peer-reviewed sources for a stock fact (corpus_adequacy_gate.py:39) â€” it either aborts as abort_corpus_inadequate or force-fits a 3-6 section clinical-shaped report (multi_section_generator.py:517) whose sentences have no grounding evidence (strict_verify drops them -> abort_no_verified_sections, CLAUDE.md Â§9.3). Critically, NOTHING accounts for stock splits, so even if prose is emitted it is a wrong/ungrounded answer. For real users at full cap this is a cost+latency blowup AND a correctness failure on the easiest class of question. Honest scope: the locked benchmark only ever feeds run_one_query 5 heavyweight DRB-EN clinical/policy questions (run_gate_b.py:723), so the locked benchmark itself is NOT broken by this; the failure surfaces for arbitrary real-user queries via the general sweep or the pipeline-B UI.
SEVERITY: P1
PROPOSED_FIX: Wire a cheap pre-generation complexity router into run_one_query, BEFORE retrieval. Step 1: lift the existing complexity signal â€” call the already-built run_scope() classifier (scope.py, returns 'simple'/'moderate'/'complex' + estimated_depth) or a deterministic heuristic (named entity + temporal range + price/quantity cue and no comparison/mechanism intent = 'simple') as an ADVISORY field on the protocol, env-gated (PG_COMPLEXITY_ROUTING, fail-open). Step 2: when complexity=='simple', branch run_one_query to a right-sized answer shape: lower PG_SWEEP_FETCH_CAP (e.g. 40), relax the adequacy gate to allow a short grounded answer instead of abort_corpus_inadequate, and let the generator emit a 1-section direct answer rather than force-flooring 3 sections. Step 3: for the financial example specifically, the right-sized answer MUST carry a split-adjustment note as a required-entity in the answer contract. Keep strict_verify / provenance tokens / 4-role gating UNCHANGED on whatever prose is emitted (faithfulness invariant intact). All gated behind a default-OFF flag so the locked 5-question benchmark stays byte-identical; activate in the general/real-user path.
SMOKE_TEST: Offline, no spend: static config-invariance assertion. Build two query dicts of wildly different complexity (a one-line 'X stock price over 20 years' vs a multi-hop clinical question), drive them through the pre-generation scope/contract resolution, and assert that the resolved section floor (3), fetch cap, and adequacy thresholds come out BYTE-IDENTICAL for both â€” proving nothing reads a complexity signal today. After the fix, the same test asserts the 'simple' query resolves to a lower fetch cap + 1-section shape + relaxed adequacy while the complex query is unchanged. Second cheap check: grep the run_one_query call graph for any read of a 'complexity'/'estimated_depth' field between scope and generation â€” currently zero hits (confirms the gap); after fix, exactly one gated read.
EVIDENCE_AUDIT: Per CLAUDE.md Â§-1.1, audit the END RESULT claim-by-claim, not metadata. Run the simple query ('Telus and Bell stock price over the past 20 years') through run_one_query and capture report.md + manifest.json + four_role_claim_audit.json. Then for EACH generated sentence: (1) read its [#ev:<id>:<start>-<end>] provenance token, (2) fetch the exact cited span from the evidence pool, (3) verify claim-vs-span line by line â€” does the cited source actually state that price, and is it split-ADJUSTED? Per-sentence verdict VERIFIED/PARTIAL/UNSUPPORTED/FABRICATED/UNREACHABLE with the quoted span. Expected for the current heavyweight path: a wave of UNSUPPORTED/UNREACHABLE verdicts (clinical-style retrieval surfaces no source grounding a split-adjusted stock price), OR the whole run lands at abort_no_verified_sections / abort_corpus_inadequate. Specifically audit any sentence stating a raw historical price for the split-adjustment fabrication: if the source quotes an unadjusted nominal price and the report presents it as a comparable 20-year series, that is a FABRICATED comparison (lethal-class per Â§-1.1 framing â€” wrong number presented as fact). This line-by-line result IS the proof that forcing the heavyweight shape on a simple query yields a wrong/ungrounded answer; it must NOT be replaced by a citation-count or 'does the report mention splits?' string-presence check.

 succeeded in 2334ms:
1:"""
2:Corpus-adequacy gate — HONEST-REBUILD R-6 Gap-1.
3:
4:Decides whether the retrieved+classified corpus is strong enough for
5:synthesis. Prevents the silent failure mode where the pipeline ships a
6:150-word report with a "13/13 rule checks pass" badge even though the
7:corpus had 3 T1 sources and a 400-word report is misleadingly brief.
8:
9:DECISION SPACE:
10:    PROCEED: corpus meets domain thresholds; synthesize normally
11:    EXPAND:  corpus short of thresholds but close; run a second
12:             retrieval round with broader queries (caller decides)
13:    ABORT:   corpus is too thin for confident synthesis; caller should
14:             either abort, ask the user to approve a short report, or
15:             widen retrieval significantly
16:
17:DOES NOT MAKE NETWORK CALLS. Pure function — tier counts + thresholds.
18:"""
19:from __future__ import annotations
20:
21:import logging
22:import os
23:from dataclasses import asdict, dataclass, field
24:from typing import Any, Literal
25:
26:logger = logging.getLogger("polaris_graph.corpus_adequacy_gate")
27:
28:
29:AdequacyDecision = Literal["proceed", "expand", "abort"]
30:
31:
32:@dataclass
33:class AdequacyThresholds:
34:    """Per-domain thresholds for corpus adequacy.
35:
36:    Loaded from the scope template's `corpus_adequacy` block. Callers
37:    can also provide overrides.
38:    """
39:    min_total_sources: int = 8
40:    min_t1_count: int = 2            # at least 2 peer-reviewed primary
41:    min_t1_plus_t2: int = 3          # or 3 combined T1+T2+T3
42:    min_t1_plus_t2_plus_t3: int = 3
43:    min_t3_plus_t4_plus_t6: int = 0  # GH#405: emerging-policy quality floor
44:    min_evidence_rows: int = 5       # after content-starved filter
45:    max_t5_plus_t6_fraction: float = 0.70   # too much industry/commentary = abort
46:    max_t7_fraction: float = 0.50           # too many stubs = abort
47:    # Fraction-of-threshold below which we ABORT instead of EXPAND
48:    abort_if_below_fraction: float = 0.5
49:
50:
51:@dataclass
52:class AdequacyFinding:
53:    name: str
54:    ok: bool
55:    observed: float
56:    threshold: float
57:    severity: str   # "ok" | "warn" | "critical"
58:
59:
60:@dataclass
61:class CorpusAdequacyReport:
62:    decision: AdequacyDecision
63:    findings: list[AdequacyFinding] = field(default_factory=list)
64:    total_sources: int = 0
65:    tier_counts: dict[str, int] = field(default_factory=dict)
66:    evidence_rows: int = 0
67:    notes: list[str] = field(default_factory=list)
68:    thresholds: dict[str, Any] = field(default_factory=dict)
69:
70:
71:_DEFAULT_DOMAIN_THRESHOLDS: dict[str, AdequacyThresholds] = {
72:    "clinical": AdequacyThresholds(
73:        min_total_sources=10, min_t1_count=3,
74:        min_t1_plus_t2=5, min_t1_plus_t2_plus_t3=6,
75:        min_evidence_rows=6,
76:        max_t5_plus_t6_fraction=0.50,
77:        max_t7_fraction=0.40,
78:    ),
79:    "policy": AdequacyThresholds(

139:def _get_thresholds(
140:    domain: str,
141:    protocol: dict[str, Any] | None = None,
142:    override: AdequacyThresholds | None = None,
143:) -> AdequacyThresholds:
144:    """Resolve adequacy thresholds with override > protocol > default."""
145:    if override is not None:
146:        return override
147:    # Protocol may carry a corpus_adequacy block
148:    if protocol:
149:        ca = protocol.get("corpus_adequacy") or {}
150:        if ca:

152:            # Merge: take protocol values where present
153:            return AdequacyThresholds(
154:                min_total_sources=int(ca.get("min_total_sources", base.min_total_sources)),
155:                min_t1_count=int(ca.get("min_t1_count", base.min_t1_count)),
156:                min_t1_plus_t2=int(ca.get("min_t1_plus_t2", base.min_t1_plus_t2)),
157:                min_t1_plus_t2_plus_t3=int(ca.get("min_t1_plus_t2_plus_t3", base.min_t1_plus_t2_plus_t3)),
158:                min_t3_plus_t4_plus_t6=int(ca.get("min_t3_plus_t4_plus_t6", base.min_t3_plus_t4_plus_t6)),
159:                min_evidence_rows=int(ca.get("min_evidence_rows", base.min_evidence_rows)),
160:                max_t5_plus_t6_fraction=float(ca.get("max_t5_plus_t6_fraction", base.max_t5_plus_t6_fraction)),
161:                max_t7_fraction=float(ca.get("max_t7_fraction", base.max_t7_fraction)),
162:                abort_if_below_fraction=float(ca.get("abort_if_below_fraction", base.abort_if_below_fraction)),
163:            )
164:    return _DEFAULT_DOMAIN_THRESHOLDS.get(domain, AdequacyThresholds())

167:def assess_corpus_adequacy(
168:    *,
169:    tier_counts: dict[str, int],
170:    evidence_row_count: int,
171:    domain: str,
172:    protocol: dict[str, Any] | None = None,
173:    override: AdequacyThresholds | None = None,
174:) -> CorpusAdequacyReport:
175:    """Return an AdequacyReport for the retrieved corpus.
176:
177:    Args:
178:        tier_counts: dict mapping "T1"/"T2"/.../"T7"/"UNKNOWN" -> count.
179:        evidence_row_count: number of evidence rows AFTER content-starved
180:            filtering (Fix-D).
181:        domain: clinical / policy / tech / due_diligence.
182:        protocol: dict form of protocol.json (may carry adequacy overrides).
183:        override: explicit AdequacyThresholds, wins over all else.
184:    """
185:    thr = _get_thresholds(domain, protocol, override)
186:
187:    total = sum(tier_counts.values())
188:    t1 = tier_counts.get("T1", 0)
189:    t2 = tier_counts.get("T2", 0)
190:    t3 = tier_counts.get("T3", 0)
191:    t4 = tier_counts.get("T4", 0)
192:    t5 = tier_counts.get("T5", 0)
193:    t6 = tier_counts.get("T6", 0)
194:    t7 = tier_counts.get("T7", 0)
195:
196:    findings: list[AdequacyFinding] = []
197:
198:    def _record(name: str, observed: float, threshold: float,
199:                direction: str, critical_at: float | None = None) -> None:
200:        if direction == "min":
201:            ok = observed >= threshold
202:            # below 50% of threshold = critical
203:            if critical_at is None:
204:                critical_at = threshold * thr.abort_if_below_fraction
205:            severity = ("ok" if ok else
206:                        "critical" if observed <= critical_at else
207:                        "warn")
208:        else:  # "max"
209:            ok = observed <= threshold
210:            # 1.5x over = critical
211:            if critical_at is None:
212:                critical_at = threshold * 1.5
213:            severity = ("ok" if ok else
214:                        "critical" if observed >= critical_at else
215:                        "warn")
216:        findings.append(AdequacyFinding(
217:            name=name, ok=ok, observed=observed,
218:            threshold=threshold, severity=severity,
219:        ))

The sweep path confirms the important seam: `run_one_query` reads the deterministic scope protocol, then later reads `PG_SWEEP_FETCH_CAP` and passes it into `run_live_retrieval`; there is no complexity-dependent branch in that interval. The adequacy gate already accepts protocol-level threshold overrides, which makes the proposed relaxed-simple profile a low-friction change.

.codex\I-ready-006\codex_brief_verdict.txt:1218:LATEST_BEST_PRACTICE: 2026 SOTA is Adaptive-RAG style query-complexity routing: a lightweight classifier tags each query (single-hop/factual vs multi-hop/complex) and routes to a right-sized pipeline â€” NaiveRAG/direct-answer for simple, full iterative/agentic/graph arsenal only when needed. 654:def preflight_import_time_constants() -> None:
655:    """FAIL CLOSED if an IMPORT-TIME module constant is below its full-capability floor — the regression
656:    guard for the import-order bug (Codex diff-gate iter-2 P1-2). ``live_retriever`` /``state`` cache
657:    ``PG_LIVE_CONTENT_MAX`` / ``PG_LIVE_HTTP_TIMEOUT`` / ``PG_AGENTIC_WEB_PER_ROUND`` at IMPORT, so reading
658:    os.getenv is NOT enough — if the slate ran AFTER the import the env is right but the constant is stale.
659:
660:    Called ONLY on the REAL CLI path (``main()``), AFTER ``load_locked_questions()`` has done the import
661:    with the slate already applied — so it validates the production import order. It is intentionally NOT
662:    in ``preflight_full_capability`` (which tests call): in a pytest process those modules are pre-imported
663:    with defaults, which is a test artifact, not a production throttle."""
664:    import importlib
665:    for module_path, attr, floor in _BENCHMARK_IMPORT_TIME_CONSTANT_FLOORS:
666:        try:
667:            mod = importlib.import_module(module_path)
668:            eff = float(getattr(mod, attr))
669:        except (ImportError, AttributeError, TypeError, ValueError) as exc:
670:            raise RuntimeError(f"benchmark preflight: cannot read {module_path}.{attr}: {exc}")
671:        if eff < floor:
672:            raise RuntimeError(
673:                f"benchmark preflight FAILED: {module_path}.{attr}={eff:g} < full-capability floor "
674:                f"{floor} — the slate was applied AFTER that module was imported, so the import-time "
675:                f"constant is STALE. Apply the slate before that import (it runs before "
676:                f"load_locked_questions in main())."
677:            )

1932:            def _planner_llm(prompt: str) -> str:
1933:                # Production Writer call. Build + smoke NEVER reach this path
1934:                # (the planner callable is injected/faked there). One Writer
1935:                # call (plus at most one bounded retry inside plan_research).
1936:                #
1937:                # `run_one_query` is async — the sweep event loop is already
1938:                # running here — so the coroutine is driven on a SEPARATE
1939:                # thread with its own loop (thread-safe; never touches the
1940:                # running loop, which `run_until_complete` would crash on).
1941:                #
1942:                # I-meta-005 Phase 1 FIX 3 (Codex diff-gate iter-1 P1 #3): the
1943:                # prior bare `ThreadPoolExecutor(...).submit(asyncio.run, ...)`
1944:                # ran with the worker's OWN empty ContextVar state, so the
1945:                # planner Writer call's billed cost accumulated in
1946:                # `_RUN_COST_CTX` only inside the worker snapshot and was LOST
1947:                # to the parent run (`current_run_cost()` / `manifest.cost_usd`
1948:                # under-reported live planner spend — a budget-cap integrity
1949:                # LAW violation). Fix mirrors `auto_induction.llm_inductor`
1950:                # rounds 3-4 (and `scope_classifier_llm._run_async_in_isolated_
1951:                # thread`): capture the parent context with
1952:                # `contextvars.copy_context()` and run the worker inside that
1953:                # snapshot via `parent_ctx.run()` (READ visibility), THEN apply
1954:                # the worker's cost delta back to the parent context via a
1955:                # closure-shared holder (write-back, fires whether or not the
1956:                # call raised — the OpenRouter client bills partial cost before
1957:                # raising on empty-content/retry).
1958:                import asyncio as _asyncio
1959:                import concurrent.futures as _futures
1960:                import contextvars as _contextvars
1961:                from src.polaris_graph.llm.openrouter_client import (
1962:                    _RUN_COST_CTX,
1963:                )
1964:
1965:                _parent_cost_before = _RUN_COST_CTX.get()
1966:                _worker_cost_after_holder: list[float] = [_parent_cost_before]
1967:
1968:                async def _run() -> str:
1969:                    _client = OpenRouterClient(model=PG_GENERATOR_MODEL)
1970:                    try:
1971:                        _resp = await _client.generate(
1972:                            prompt=prompt, max_tokens=2000, temperature=0.2,
1973:                        )
1974:                        return (_resp.content or "").strip()
1975:                    finally:
1976:                        # Capture the worker snapshot's accumulated cost even
1977:                        # on raise (OpenRouter bills partial cost before
1978:                        # raising on empty-content/retry paths).
1979:                        _worker_cost_after_holder[0] = _RUN_COST_CTX.get()
1980:                        if hasattr(_client, "close"):
1981:                            try:
1982:                                await _client.close()
1983:                            except Exception:
1984:                                pass
1985:
1986:                _parent_ctx = _contextvars.copy_context()
1987:
1988:                def _worker() -> str:
1989:                    def _run_under_ctx() -> str:
1990:                        return _asyncio.run(_run())
1991:                    return _parent_ctx.run(_run_under_ctx)
1992:
1993:                try:
1994:                    with _futures.ThreadPoolExecutor(max_workers=1) as _pool:
1995:                        return _pool.submit(_worker).result()
1996:                finally:
1997:                    # Apply the worker's cost delta to the parent context so
1998:                    # the planner Writer spend merges into the parent run cost
1999:                    # (whether or not the worker raised).
2000:                    _cost_delta = (
2001:                        _worker_cost_after_holder[0] - _parent_cost_before
2002:                    )
2003:                    if _cost_delta > 0:
2004:                        _RUN_COST_CTX.set(_parent_cost_before + _cost_delta)
2005:

codex
The named expensive features are not all controlled by `fetch_cap`: STORM can spend before retrieval, and agentic can spend after retrieval if its flag is on. Because the brief frames fetch cap as the primary fix and leaves verification intact, I’m treating this as residual scope unless it blocks the requested failure mode.

1:"""Sweep-side adapter for the citation-snowball evidence_deepener (I-meta-002-q1d #942-deepener).
2:
3:Wires POLARIS's frontier-grade `evidence_deepener` (backward+forward S2 citation chase + recommendations
4:+ mechanism search) into the launch sweep behind a flag + a Stop-RAG value-based trigger. SAFETY DESIGN
5:(Codex brief-gate, Option A): the deepener only DISCOVERS relevant primary-paper URLs; those URLs are then
6:fed back through the EXISTING `run_live_retrieval(seed_urls=...)` chokepoint (fetch → classify_source_tier
7:→ is_content_starved → _build_provenance_quote), so a deepened paper earns its tier ONLY from fetched
8:content and a thin/abstract-only paper is DROPPED fail-closed — no tier laundering, zero new evidence-row
9:build logic that could drift from strict_verify.
10:
11:Pure orchestration helpers (no I/O except the injected `deepen_evidence` coroutine). The sweep does the
12:merge + the `run_live_retrieval` pass; this module only builds the deepener state, runs the coroutine
13:safely from a sync caller, applies the trigger predicate, and extracts the discovered URLs.
14:"""

23:# Model the deepener uses for its mechanism-query generation LLM call (env-overridable).
24:DEEPENER_LLM_MODEL = os.getenv("PG_SWEEP_DEEPENER_MODEL", "deepseek/deepseek-v4-pro")

30:def should_trigger_deepener(
31:    *,
32:    flag_on: bool,
33:    has_s2_key: bool,
34:    has_seed_evidence: bool,
35:    adequacy_decision: str,
36:    total_uncovered: int,
37:) -> bool:
38:    """Stop-RAG value-based trigger (Codex brief-gate iter-1 required predicate). The deepener fires
39:    ONLY when it is enabled AND there is something to chase from AND the corpus is BORDERLINE — i.e.
40:    NOT on an already-comfortably-adequate corpus with full coverage.
41:
42:    - `flag_on`: PG_SWEEP_EVIDENCE_DEEPENER truthy (default OFF — the deepener SPENDS).
43:    - `has_s2_key`: SEMANTIC_SCHOLAR_API_KEY present (the deepener no-ops without it).
44:    - `has_seed_evidence`: there is existing evidence to chase citations FROM (else "abort-impossible").
45:    - borderline := adequacy.decision != "proceed" (i.e. "expand"/"abort") OR post-R6 uncovered topics > 0.
46:    """
47:    if not (flag_on and has_s2_key and has_seed_evidence):
48:        return False
49:    return adequacy_decision != "proceed" or total_uncovered > 0

52:def build_deepener_state(evidence_rows: list[dict[str, Any]], question: str) -> dict[str, Any]:
53:    """Build the 3-key state the deepener reads (`iteration_count`, `evidence` carrying `source_url`,
54:    `original_query`). Pure."""
55:    evidence = []
56:    for ev in evidence_rows or []:
57:        # Strip BEFORE the blank check (Codex diff-gate iter-1 P1): a whitespace-only url is not seed
58:        # evidence.
59:        url = (ev.get("source_url") or ev.get("url") or "").strip()
60:        if url:
61:            evidence.append({"source_url": url})
62:    return {"iteration_count": 0, "evidence": evidence, "original_query": question or ""}
63:
64:
65:def run_deepener_sync(
66:    state: dict[str, Any],
67:    *,
68:    deepen_fn: Callable[[dict[str, Any]], Awaitable[dict[str, Any]]] | None = None,
69:) -> dict[str, Any]:
70:    """Run the async `deepen_evidence` coroutine from a SYNC caller WITHOUT raising RuntimeError if an
71:    event loop is already running (Codex brief-gate iter-1 P1). Normal sweep execution has no running
72:    loop → `asyncio.run`. If a loop IS running (async test harness / embedded caller), run the coroutine
73:    in an ISOLATED thread with its own loop so it fails closed locally and never aborts unrelated work.
74:
75:    `deepen_fn` is injectable so offline tests pass a FAKE deepener (no network/spend). The REAL
76:    `deepen_evidence(client, state)` takes an OpenRouterClient FIRST (Codex diff-gate iter-2 P1) — the
77:    default closure constructs one and adapts it to the 1-arg `fn(state)` interface used here.
78:    """
79:    if deepen_fn is None:
80:        from src.polaris_graph.agents.evidence_deepener import deepen_evidence  # noqa: E402
81:        from src.polaris_graph.llm.openrouter_client import OpenRouterClient  # noqa: E402
82:
83:        async def deepen_fn(_state: dict[str, Any]) -> dict[str, Any]:
84:            # Close the client after the pass to avoid leaking its async HTTP client (Codex diff-gate
85:            # iter-3 P2; mirrors the generator pattern, e.g. analyst_synthesis).
86:            client = OpenRouterClient(model=DEEPENER_LLM_MODEL)
87:            try:
88:                return await deepen_evidence(client, _state)
89:            finally:
90:                await client.close()
91:
92:    try:
93:        asyncio.get_running_loop()
94:        loop_running = True
95:    except RuntimeError:
96:        loop_running = False
97:
98:    if loop_running:
99:        with concurrent.futures.ThreadPoolExecutor(max_workers=1) as executor:
100:            return executor.submit(lambda: asyncio.run(deepen_fn(state))).result()
101:    return asyncio.run(deepen_fn(state))
102:
103:
104:def discovered_urls(deepener_output: dict[str, Any] | None, *, cap: int = DEFAULT_DEEPENER_URL_CAP) -> list[str]:
105:    """Extract de-duplicated, non-blank discovered paper URLs from the deepener output, capped. These
106:    are seeded into the `run_live_retrieval(seed_urls=...)` chokepoint (not turned into evidence rows
107:    here — the existing fetch/tier/provenance pipeline does that)."""
108:    # Exact cap (Codex diff-gate iter-1 P1): a non-positive cap yields NO urls (and never flows a
109:    # negative into fetch_cap) — guard up front so the append-then-break can't return one url at cap=0.
110:    if cap is None or cap <= 0:
111:        return []
112:    papers = (deepener_output or {}).get("deepened_papers", []) or []
113:    out: list[str] = []
114:    seen: set[str] = set()
115:    for paper in papers:
116:        url = (paper.get("url") or "").strip() if isinstance(paper, dict) else ""
117:        if not url or url in seen:
118:            continue
119:        seen.add(url)
120:        out.append(url)
121:        if len(out) >= cap:
122:            break
123:    return out

Trigger vocabulary (any of, case-insensitive): "mechanism", "pharmacokinetic", "pharmacodynamic", "receptor", "half-life", "bioavailability", "metabolism", "agonist", "antagonist", "binding", "signaling", "pathway", "kinetic". A research-grade synthesis explains WHY the intervention works, not only WHETHER it works. Top-tier Deep Research outputs (GPT-5.4 DR, Gemini 3.1 Pro DR) dedicate a full section to mechanism/pharmacology for any clinical efficacy question; a report without it reads as a short brief rather than a deep synthesis. This rule is generalizable: in materials/chemistry a Mechanism section covers reaction pathway / phase transition / interface chemistry; in policy it covers causal pathway / incentive mechanism / enforcement mechanism; in finance it covers transmission channel / market microstructure.

99:@dataclass
100:class InclusionExclusionCriteria:
101:    """PRISMA-style inclusion / exclusion criteria."""
102:
103:    inclusion: list[str] = field(default_factory=list)
104:    exclusion: list[str] = field(default_factory=list)
105:
106:    def normalize(self) -> "InclusionExclusionCriteria":
107:        """Deduplicate and trim."""
108:        inc = sorted({i.strip() for i in self.inclusion if i.strip()})
109:        exc = sorted({e.strip() for e in self.exclusion if e.strip()})
110:        return InclusionExclusionCriteria(inclusion=inc, exclusion=exc)

2:pipeline_a_ui_adapter — BUG-B-102 R2c (pipeline-B UI parity via pipeline-A).
3:
4:The Docker default `serve` path (scripts/live_server.py → FastAPI) has
5:three legacy graph variants (v1/v2/v3) that do NOT enforce any of the
6:5-round pipeline-A hardening (strict_verify, corpus_approval,
7:delimiter sanitization, abort statuses, two-family evaluator).
8:Codex full-audit pass 1 flagged this as a blocker (B-102).
9:
10:v4 is a thin shim: it accepts the v1/v2/v3 UI signature, synthesizes a
11:pipeline-A query dict, calls `scripts.run_honest_sweep_r3.run_one_query`
12:(the battle-tested, 10+ rounds-hardened orchestrator), then adapts the
13:pipeline-A manifest + report into the UI's JSON contract at
14:`outputs/polaris_graph/{vector_id}.json`.
15:
16:Trace events (`pipeline_start`, `report_assembled`, `pipeline_end`)
17:are emitted through the existing PipelineTracer so the live_server
18:SSE endpoint keeps working without frontend changes.
19:
20:Design choices:
21:- No refactor of run_one_query. Call it as-is with a synthesized `q`.
22:- Domain inference: if the caller's `application` field matches a known
23:  domain key, use it; else default to "custom" (see R2b scope template).
24:- No forced amplification — UI queries come in raw; the retriever will
25:  do whatever query amplification it normally does.
26:- Pipeline-A artifacts go to a run directory; a pointer is added to
27:  the UI JSON so consumers can drill down.

41:_DOC_ID_RE = re.compile(r"[a-f0-9]{16}")
42:
43:
44:def _load_uploaded_documents(
45:    document_ids: list[str], ingester: Any = None, chunk_size: int = 1500,
46:) -> list[dict]:
47:    """Load chunks for given document_ids from DocumentIngester.
48:
49:    Per I-f3-001. Validates each doc_id against 16-hex format (matches
50:    `hashlib.sha256(file_bytes).hexdigest()[:16]` per document_ingester.py:162)
51:    BEFORE filesystem lookup to prevent path traversal. Skips invalid /
52:    missing IDs with a logged warning. Raises RuntimeError if every
53:    requested ID failed (LAW II — fail loud).
54:    """
55:    if not document_ids:
56:        return []
57:    if ingester is None:
58:        from src.polaris_graph.document_ingester import DocumentIngester
59:        ingester = DocumentIngester()
60:    out: list[dict] = []
61:    for doc_id in document_ids:
62:        if not _DOC_ID_RE.fullmatch(doc_id):
63:            logger.warning("[v4 graph] invalid doc_id format: %r", doc_id)
64:            continue
65:        doc = ingester.get_document(doc_id)
66:        if doc is None:
67:            logger.warning("[v4 graph] doc_id %s not found", doc_id)
68:            continue
69:        content = doc.get("content", "")
70:        if not content:
71:            logger.warning("[v4 graph] doc_id %s has empty content", doc_id)
72:            continue
73:        meta = doc.get("metadata", {})
74:        name = meta.get("original_filename") or meta.get("filename") or doc_id
75:        chunks = [content[i : i + chunk_size] for i in range(0, len(content), chunk_size)]
76:        for idx, chunk_text in enumerate(chunks):
77:            out.append({
78:                "document_id": doc_id, "filename": name,
79:                "chunk_index": idx, "text": chunk_text,
80:            })
81:    if not out:
82:        raise RuntimeError(
83:            f"_load_uploaded_documents: every requested document_id "
84:            f"({len(document_ids)} ids) failed to resolve"
85:        )
86:    return out

112:def _infer_domain(application: str, query: str) -> str:
113:    """Return a scope-template domain. Default to 'custom' for
114:    free-form UI queries that don't hint at clinical/tech/policy/dd."""
115:    a = (application or "").lower()
116:    if a in _DOMAIN_HINTS:
117:        return _DOMAIN_HINTS[a]
118:    q = (query or "").lower()
119:    for key, dom in _DOMAIN_HINTS.items():
120:        if key in q:
121:            return dom
122:    return "custom"

125:def _safe_load_json(path: Path) -> dict[str, Any]:
126:    """Best-effort JSON load; empty dict if missing / malformed."""
127:    if not path.exists():
128:        return {}
129:    try:
130:        return json.loads(path.read_text(encoding="utf-8"))
131:    except Exception:
132:        return {}

# Custom / free-form scope template — BUG-B-102 R2b (pipeline-B UI path).
#
# Used when the caller (typically scripts/live_server.py → graph_v4
# UI research endpoint) submits a research question that doesn't fit
# the four core domain templates (clinical, tech, policy, due_diligence).
# The template is deliberately permissive on tier distribution because
# free-form UI queries span topic domains where enforcing a specific
# tier mix would be incorrect.
#
# IMPORTANT: this does NOT disable the hardening invariants. The
# corpus_adequacy_gate, strict_verify, evaluator gate, and delimiter
# sanitization all still fire. It only loosens the tier-distribution
# *expectation* so corpus_approval_gate doesn't auto-reject a diverse
# UI-query corpus.

domain: custom
description: >
  Free-form scope template for UI-submitted research questions that
  don't match clinical / tech / policy / due_diligence. Treats any
  classified source tier as acceptable; the corpus-approval gate
  relies on the operator's substantive note for quality control.

inclusion_criteria:
  - Any source classified at T1-T7 by the tier classifier.
  - Official documentation with clear authorship.
  - Primary-source reporting from reputable outlets.

exclusion_criteria:
  - Unattributed AI-generated summaries.
  - Content-starved URLs (below PG_CRAG_PAYWALL_MIN_CHARS).
  - Known disinformation or retracted sources (per RetractionWatch).

expected_tier_distribution:
  # Intentionally broad. No tier has a mandatory minimum because the
  # UI caller may legitimately submit questions where T1 primary
  # research simply doesn't exist (consumer tech, recent events).
  - tier: T1
    min_fraction: 0.00
    max_fraction: 0.70
    rationale: >
      Peer-reviewed research preferred when topic permits.
  - tier: T2
    min_fraction: 0.00
    max_fraction: 0.50
    rationale: >
      Systematic reviews and meta-analyses.
  - tier: T3
    min_fraction: 0.00
    max_fraction: 0.50
    rationale: >
      Government / regulatory / standards bodies.
  - tier: T4
    min_fraction: 0.00
    max_fraction: 0.50
    rationale: >
      Preprints and working papers.
  - tier: T5
    min_fraction: 0.00
    max_fraction: 0.50

25:## Finding (`.codex/I-ready-000/findings/query_complexity_routing.md`, P1)
26:POLARIS applies an IDENTICAL heavyweight deep-research shape to EVERY query — no code path reads a
27:query-complexity signal between intake and generation. A simple factual query ("Telus and Bell stock
28:price over 20 years") is forced down the full heavyweight path: the I-cap-005 slate force-ONs
29:PG_SWEEP_FETCH_CAP=1000, STORM, agentic URL-discovery, the deepener, 4-role per-claim verification,
30:$25/run — then the clinical adequacy gate (min 8 sources / 2 T1) can't surface peer-reviewed sources
31:for a stock fact, so it aborts `abort_corpus_inadequate` OR force-fits a 3-6 section clinical-shaped
32:report whose ungrounded sentences strict_verify drops (`abort_no_verified_sections`). A cost+latency
33:blowup AND a correctness failure on the easiest class of question.
34:
35:**Honest scope (not over-claimed):** the LOCKED 5-question DRB-EN benchmark is NOT broken by this (all
36:5 are heavyweight clinical/policy). The failure surfaces for arbitrary real-user queries via the
37:general sweep / pipeline-B UI. So this MUST be default-OFF (locked benchmark byte-identical) and
38:activated on the general/real-user path.
39:
40:## Current state (verified file:line)
41:- `run_one_query` scopes every query via the deterministic `run_scope_gate`
42:  (`run_honest_sweep_r3.py:1674` → `protocol = scope.protocol.to_json_dict()` :1680). No complexity
43:  classification; nothing varies depth/shape by difficulty.
44:- `_fetch_cap = int(os.getenv("PG_SWEEP_FETCH_CAP", "40"))` at `:1898`; used by `run_live_retrieval`
45:  at `:2268`.
46:- `corpus_adequacy_gate.py:33 AdequacyThresholds` (min_total_sources=8, min_t1_count=2; per-domain
47:  variants :73/84/92/99/109) — no "simple factual query, a short answer is fine" branch.
48:- Generator hard-floors >=3 sections (`multi_section_generator.py:517-518 section_count_below_min`).
49:- A built-but-unwired LLM complexity classifier exists (`nodes/scope.py run_scope()` →
50:  simple/moderate/complex + estimated_depth) but is LLM-based and wired ONLY to graph_v3 (pipeline-B),
51:  absent from the benchmark path.
52:
53:## Proposed scope (route the granularity decisions to you)
54:
55:**Classifier — DETERMINISTIC, not the LLM run_scope() (DECISION 1 for you):** I propose a cheap
56:deterministic heuristic (new module `src/polaris_graph/nodes/complexity_router.py`): a query is
57:`simple` iff it has a price/quantity/factual cue + a named entity + (optional) a temporal range AND
58:NO comparison/mechanism/causal/synthesis intent; else `complex`; `moderate` between. Returns
59:`(complexity, confidence, reasons)`. WHY deterministic over run_scope(): (a) §8.4 — run_scope() is an
60:LLM call; burning an LLM call just to decide a query is simple is self-defeating for a cost-saving
61:feature; (b) offline-testable, zero spend, deterministic. Your call if you'd prefer run_scope().
62:
63:**Wiring — flag-gated, fail-open:** call the classifier in `run_one_query` AFTER the scope-gate
64:(:1680) and BEFORE the fetch-cap read (:1898), gated `PG_COMPLEXITY_ROUTING` (default OFF →
65:byte-identical). **FAIL-OPEN**: any classifier error OR `confidence < PG_COMPLEXITY_MIN_CONFIDENCE`
66:OR complexity != "simple" → the FULL heavyweight path (never under-serve a complex/clinical query).
67:Emit a `complexity_routing` manifest field (complexity, confidence, reasons, applied:bool) — the
68:routing decision is auditable.
69:
70:**Right-sizing for `simple` (DECISION 2 for you — scope granularity):** when complexity=="simple"
71:AND routing ON AND confident:
72:- (a) lower the fetch cap: `_fetch_cap = int(os.getenv("PG_SIMPLE_FETCH_CAP", "40"))` instead of the
73:  1000 slate value — fixes the PRIMARY cost/latency blowup. [low risk]
74:- (b) a "simple" adequacy profile so a short grounded answer is allowed instead of
75:  `abort_corpus_inadequate` (e.g. min_total_sources=1, min_t1_count=0 for simple). [faithfulness-
76:  adjacent — but strict_verify + 4-role still drop ungrounded sentences, so a relaxed-adequacy simple
77:  query can ship ONLY grounded prose or lands at abort_no_verified_sections; faithfulness intact.]
78:- (c) allow a 1-section direct answer (relax the >=3 section floor for simple). [secondary]
79:My lean: ship (a)+(b) (the cost fix + the right-sized-answer enabler) in this PR; (c) section-floor
80:is a smaller follow-up if it bloats the diff past the 200-LOC cap. Your call on whether to include
81:(c) and on the (b) adequacy-relaxation safety.
82:
83:**FAITHFULNESS INVARIANT (unchanged):** strict_verify per-sentence provenance + the 4-role D8 binding
84:gate + provenance-token enforcement are NOT touched. The router only changes WHICH path/thresholds a
85:classified-simple query takes; every emitted sentence is still verified identically.
86:
87:**Financial split-adjustment (DECISION 3 — defer?):** the finding wants the simple financial answer
88:to carry a split-adjustment required-entity. That is a domain-specific answer-contract addition; I
89:propose DEFERRING it to a follow-up (it needs a financial answer-contract + a stock-split data
90:source) and keeping #1082 to the general complexity router. Confirm.
